3.2.1  Identification of and Response to Climate Change 
Opportunities
In response to the possible risks and impact of climate change, FPC regularly convenes meetings to review 
risks and opportunities arising from climate change each year. FPC also draws up and implements response 
and prevention measures in advance by referencing the Task Force on Climate-Related Financial Disclosures 
(TCFD) issued by the Financial Stability Board with a view to reducing the impact of climate change on FPC.
Sustainable Development Website: 2022 Task Force on 
Climate-Related Financial Disclosures
Governance
Strategy
Management 
Strategy and 
Action Plan
 The Board of Directors shall be the highest 
decision-making and supervisory unit of the 
Company in response to climate change, 
and the Chairman of the Board of Directors 
shall be the highest manager responsible for 
supervising issues and matters related to 
climate change.
 Report the Company's climate change-
related affairs to the Board of Directors as 
an important reference for the formulation of 
sustainable policies.
 FPC has established the Energy Conservation 
and Carbon Reduction Promotion Team, 
which is responsible for promoting and 
implementing response measures on climate 
change-related issues. The Chairman 
convenes a monthly energy-saving and 
carbon-reduction team meeting to review 
the progress of energy-saving and carbon-
reduction implementation and target 
achievement.
 Coal-fired transition to low (zero) 
carbon energy: promotion of coal-to-
gas conversion, elimination of outdated 
coal-fired boilers, carbon capture and 
reuse, promotion of low-energy hydrogen 
production technologies
 Energy-saving and carbon-reducing circular 
economy: Introduce artificial intelligence (AI) 
technology for energy-saving, equipment 
upgrade/process optimization, and 
research and development of low-energy-
consumption catalysts
 Increase the use of renewable energy: Build 
solar panel power generation equipment, and 
use the Formosa Heavy Industries wind power.
 Other carbon reduction measures: use of 
biomass ethylene to produce PE, recycled 
products, application of lightweight products 
and material application of renewable 
energy equipment.
Implementation
On May 10, 2022, FPC’s Board of Directors 
approved the establishment of the Sustainable 
Development Committee to strengthen the 
responsibility of the Board of Directors for 
deliberation and supervision of sustainable 
issues such as climate change. Important 
resolutions are as follows:
(1) Adoption of internal carbon pricing
(2) Promotion of carbon reduction in the supply 
chain and establishment of the "equipment 
selection analysis table" for procurement 
projects of high-carbon emission equipment 
to incorporate carbon emission costs into 
procurement selection process
(3) Guidance on safety and health, 
environmental protection, and greenhouse 
gas reduction for downstream customers 
to assist them in achieving carbon 
management objectives
 For the implementation and progress of 
individual strategies, please refer to FPC’s 
2022 Task Force on Climate-Related Financial 
Disclosures.
 Introduction of artificial intelligence (AI) 
technology, such as using AI technology 
to adjust the bottom temperature of the 
isomer separation tower and to more 
accurately separate semi-finished products 
like n-butyraldehyde and isobutyraldehyde 
according to the difference in boiling points, 
thus in turn reducing steam consumption
 We have collaborated with academic institutions 
to research and develop carbon capture and 
reuse processes. A carbon sequestration pilot 
plant was established at the Renwu complex to 
convert CO2 in the exhaust gas generated at the 
public utilities complex into methane to be used 
as fuel for the cracking furnaces at the VCM 
plants. The testing phase has been completed 
in 2022, and from 2023 onwards, we will focus 
on the research and development of even 
more energy-saving carbon sequestration 
and alkane conversion technologies.

Risk Management
Goals and Targets
 Every six months, FPC collects, analyzes, and compiles 
information on climate change and energy risks 
and opportunities. Also, FPC formulates the Risk 
Management Procedures by referring to the principles, 
framework, and requirements of ISO 22301 to identify 
and assess climate change risks and opportunities.
 The risk matrix is used to determine significant risks 
and opportunities. The evaluation indicators include 
the degree of financial impact and the probability of 
occurrence of risks and opportunities.
FPC has set an absolute target for carbon emission 
reduction with 2020 as the base year, of which:
 Short-term reduction target: 20% reduction in 2025 
compared to the base year
 Medium-term reduction target: 40% reduction in 2030 
compared to the base year
 Long-term reduction target: Reaching carbon neutrality 
by 2050
Please refer to Chapter 3.2.1 of this Report and FPC’s 
2022 TCFD Report
In 2021, the inventory of GHG Scope 1 and Scope 2 was 
8.604 million tons of carbon dioxide equivalent, which was 
31,000 tons less than the absolute reduction target in 
2020, with a reduction ratio of 0.4%. FPC will continue to 
work on carbon reduction improvement projects, such as 
the project to utilize combustible waste gas in coal-fired 
boilers at the Linyuan PE and PP plants, which is expected 
to be completed and put into operation in 2024 to reduce 
an estimate of 44,000 tons of carbon dioxide equivalent 
per year.
 Coal-burning transition to low (zero) carbon energy: an 
estimated reduction of 674,000 tons of CO2e
 Energy saving and carbon reduction circular economy: 
an estimated reduction of 569,000 tons of CO2e
 Increase the use of renewable energy: an estimated 
reduction of 708,000 tons of CO2e
 Other carbon reduction measures: to assist the value 
chain to reduce an estimate of 5.255 million tons of CO2e

Appendix
 
Risk and Opportunity Identification Results
FPC draws a risk and opportunity matrix (as shown below) to identify climate change risks and 
opportunities according to the level of climate-related financial impact (vertical axis) and the likelihood of 
occurrence (horizontal axis). According to the risk and opportunity matrix scores, the climate-related risks 
and opportunities are classified into major risks/opportunities, medium risks/opportunities, and low risks/
opportunities. All climate change management programs are incorporated into our environment-related 
risk management system and regularly monitored.
Risk Category
FPC’s Climate Change Related Risk Management Principles
Major Risks
15~25 Points
Relevant units must establish corresponding management plans to reduce losses caused 
by risks, such as reducing the number of occurrences, reducing financial impact, risk 
shifting, and risk aversion
Medium Risks
6~14 Points
No action is required at the moment, but continuous monitoring still has to be carried out
Low risks
1~5 Points
Acceptable risks

1. Carbon Fee 
Collection
1. The “National Climate Change Action 
Guidelines” and “Climate Change Response 
Act” specify our long-term greenhouse gas 
reduction targets, and establish the total 
greenhouse gas emission control and allocation 
method for manufacturing departments.
2. The "Climate Change Response Act" will include 
major carbon emitters in the manufacturing 
industry with greenhouse gas emissions 
of more than 25,000 tons of carbon dioxide 
equivalent (CO2e) as the target for carbon fees, 
resulting in an increase in expenditure costs. 
Assuming that the cost of carbon cannot be 
transferred, product prices will become less 
competitive, resulting in a significant financial 
impact.
3. The European Union is expected to impose 
a carbon border tax starting 2026, which is 
expected to have an impact on FPC’s vinyl 
chloride (VCM) and polyvinyl chloride (PVC).
Transition 
Risk/Policy 
and Legal
Direct 
Operations
Major Risks
2. Renewable 
Energy 
Development 
Act - Setting Up 
Green Energy
The amendment to the "Renewable Energy 
Development Act" was legally passed in April 
2019. Since the contracted capacity of our 
Linyuan Complex in the amount of 25,000 kW is 
larger than the 5,000 kW required by law, FPC is 
required to install 10% of the contracted capacity 
of renewable energy equipment, energy storage 
equipment, or purchase renewable energy 
certificates within 5 years, or else we must pay a 
payment in lieu.
Transition 
Risk/Policy 
and Legal
Direct 
Operations
Medium Risks
3. Water 
Consumption 
Fee Collection
Considering the impact of water shortages due to 
climate change, in order to stabilize water supply 
and boost economic and social development in 
Taiwan, the Ministry of Economic Affairs has 
started imposing water consumption fees in 
2023. For drought seasons (January to April and 
November to December), an additional water 
consumption fee is imposed on users with water 
consumption greater than 9,000 m  in a single 
month. Currently, the monthly water consumption 
of the Mailiao, Hsinkang, and Renwu complexes 
is more than 9,000 m , and the collection of water 
consumption fees will increase operating costs.
Transition

and Legal

Response Strategy and Target
Case Example
1. FPC communicates with the government through industry 
associations (or societies) every year to develop a reasonable 
and feasible carbon emissions trading mechanism and related 
ordinances in order to create a win-win solution.
2. Coal-fired transformation towards low (zero) carbon energy: 
promote boiler fuel from coal to gas, eliminate old coal-fired 
boilers, and use low-carbon sources of electricity.
3. Energy-saving and carbon-reducing circular economy: 
Introducing smart factories (aided by AI technology, improving 
the conversion rate of raw materials, and reducing unit 
consumption), equipment upgrade/process optimization, 
research and development of low-energy-consumption catalysts 
in the process, and setting up a carbon fixation pilot plant to 
convert CO2 in exhaust gas into methane (fuel).
4. FPC has established an internal carbon pricing mechanism in 
2022. It is calculated based on the carbon fee of the Climate 
Change Response Act and the price increase of carbon emissions 
exceeding the target value. The relevant carbon costs are 
included in our internal profit and loss statements as the basis 
for implementing carbon risk management. In addition to 
continuously formulating greenhouse gas emission reduction 
measures, relevant information is also an important indicator 
for performance evaluations, product operations, investment 
assessments, etc., in order to maintain our competitiveness.
5. Target: Set GHG reduction absolute targets with 2020 as the base 
year to reduce by 20% in 2025 compared with the base year, 
reduce by 40% in 2030 compared with the base year, and achieve 
carbon neutrality by 2050.
 The energy consumption, water 
consumption and carbon dioxide emissions 
of each plant must be reported to the head 
of the water saving and energy saving unit 
on a monthly basis.
  It is estimated that by 2030, there will be a 
total investment of NT$6.98 billion in water-
saving and energy-saving improvement 
projects, of which:
(1)Promote coal-fired transition to low (zero) 
carbon energy: NT$1.37 billion
(2)Energy saving and carbon reduction 
circular economy: NT$2.49 billion
(3)Increase the amount of renewable 
energy: NT$2.18 billion
(4)Other carbon reduction measures: 
NT$940 million
1. In order to comply with regulatory requirements, FPC has 
proposed to set up a demonstration site for renewable energy 
and has conducted a preliminary assessment of the site and type 
of renewable energy to be installed. Since the main plants are 
located in the south-central part of Taiwan with strong sunlight, 
they are suitable for installing solar power generation equipment. 
After evaluation, over 5,000 kW of solar photovoltaics will be 
installed to meet the requirements of regulations.
2. FPC intends to purchase wind power and green power certificates 
from Formosa Heavy Industries Corp. again to ensure that the 
use of renewable energy is safe and in compliance with laws and 
regulations.
3. Target: By 2025, 100% of all administrative areas in all complexes 
will use renewable energy.
After assessment, the Mailiao parking 
lot area is set up as a renewable energy 
demonstration site with 4,000 kW solar 
modules to generate 5.296 million kWh of 
power annually and to reduce 4,443 tons of 
carbon annually. The construction cost is 
about NT$240,000,000.
1. In order to reduce the use of water resources, FPC reduces 
demand for water resources through source management as 
well as enhances reuse of water resources and accelerates the 
recycling treatment process at the end.
2. Target: Continue to promote the reduction of water consumption 
per unit of product by 5% compared with the average of the 
previous year.
For recycling of water discharge from 
cooling towers at the Renwu Complex, UF/
RO membranes are prone to clogging due to 
water quality characteristics. Therefore, FPC 
developed a patent that enables water quality 
to meet the UF/RO water quality standards 
upon pre-treatment. The plan is to adaptively 
reuse the existing canal water treatment 
facilities that are underutilized. We are 
conducting dosing tests and re-programming 
of physical equipment for the current survey.

4. Kaohsiung City 
Coal-reduction 
Policy
In order to achieve the goal of net zero emissions 
by 2050, the Kaohsiung City Government 
has passed the net zero city management 
autonomous regulations in October 2022. 
Furthermore, the Kaohsiung City Government 
is planning to establish targeted schedules for 
future coal reduction and replacement projects, 
gradually moving towards a coal-free city. As our 
Renwu complex generates electricity for coal-
fired boilers and sells electricity to Taipower, 
should the competent authority decided to ban 
coal burning in the future, we may see a decrease 
in our revenue.

may purchase less non-low-carbon and energy-

6. Company 
Reputation
1. In response to the boom in ESG in recent 
years, financial institutions will evaluate 
clients' ESG performance when deciding to 
invest and grant loans. If the ESG sustainability 
requirements cannot be met, in addition to the 
negative impact on the company's reputation, 
financial institutions may increase the 
borrowing rate, and in severe cases will not 
loan to high-carbon industries.
2. At the COP26 summit, 40 countries pledged 
to phasing out coal burning. FPC assessed 
that continued burning of coal would have an 
immediate impact on "reputation".

1. The climate conditions of the plant area in the 
near future (2016-2035) are estimated using 
1986-2005 as the base period. Under the RCP 4.5 
and RCP 8.5 scenarios, the maximum continuous 
rainfall is 5.9-12.9 days, and the total rainfall is 
1,017-2,373 mm. The RCP 8.5 scenario predicts 
that the number of typhoons in Taiwan is -15%, 
the proportion of strong typhoons is +100%, and 
the typhoon rainfall is +20%.
2. Due to the strong wind or typhoon impact 
caused by abnormal climate, the complex 
needs to be stopped safely to avoid process 
hazards; the impact of heavy rainfall/flood 
which causes the plant to stop due to flooding 
will result in revenue loss.

1. Since 2018, FPC has started promoting green product solutions 
and constructed green products in eight aspects, including energy 
efficiency, emission reduction, waste reduction, water saving, 
non-toxicity, health, recycled products, and safety. And from 
these eight aspects, we invest in R&D and accelerate the time of 
productization, and develop differentiated and high-value forward-
looking green products, so as to turn climate change issues into 
business opportunities to improve corporate value. For example, 
PP post-consumer recycled pellets are developed for plastic 
woven bag packaging to reduce the use of new materials and 
carbon emissions by more than 30%. Also, sugarcane and corn are 
used as raw materials of biomass ethylene to produce PE, which 
can reduce carbon footprint. FPC is committed to promoting the 
innovation and development of green products, so as to address 
environmental problems more effectively and achieve sustainable 
development.

replaced by PP woven bags made of 30% post-consumer recycled 
pellets.

is used in dashboards, panels, headlight 
inner shells, and bumpers on vehicles. 
This material can effectively reduce vehicle 
weight, energy consumption, and GHG 
emissions.

management staffs are needed for this 
project. Based on the estimated average 
monthly salary of NT$52,600 per person 
at FPC, the estimated management cost is 
NT$1,262,400/year.

organizations.

Results
The category "Environmental Natural Disasters 
- Climate and Weather" includes risks such as 
energy resource management. Taking 1986-
2005 as the base period, the climate conditions 
of the plant area in the near future (2016~2035) 
are estimated. Under the RCP 4.5 and RCP 
8.5 scenarios, the maximum continuous 
rainfall is 5.9~12.9 days, and the total rainfall 
is 1,017~2,373mm, which is a 15% increase in 
total rainfall over average. The RCP 8.5 scenario 
predicts that the number of typhoons in Taiwan 
is -15%, the proportion of strong typhoons is 
+100%, and the typhoon rainfall is +20%.
The category "Environmental Natural Disasters 
- Climate and Weather" includes risks such as 
energy resource management. Taking 1986 to 
2005 as the base period, it is estimated that the 
climate condition of the plant area in the near 
future (2016~2035) will cause water shortage or 
drought for two months every year.
Impact and 
Effects
Based on the individual turnover of NT$195.1 
billion in 2022, the estimated loss will be 
NT$534,521 thousand when the work is 
stopped for 1 day due to strong winds, 
typhoons, heavy rainfall, or flooding.
Based on the individual turnover of NT$195.1 billion 
in 2022, the estimated loss will be NT$1,594,563 
thousand when the work is stopped for 3 days due to 
water shortages/droughts.
Risks and 
Opportunities
Due to the strong wind or typhoon impact 
caused by abnormal climate, the complex 
needs to be stopped safely to avoid process 
hazards; however, the shutdown will result in 
revenue loss.
In recent years, due to the impact of global 
climate change, there have been changes in the 
wet season and precipitation in Taiwan. The start 
of the wet season has been delayed from May 
to June, and the length of the wet season has 
become shorter, resulting in decreased rainfall 
during the dry season as well as possible water 
shortages. Therefore, it is necessary to secure 
additional water supply from other sources. If the 
complexes are shut down due to water shortages, 
we will experience a turnover loss.
Action Plan
In response to the potential risks caused by 
strong winds or typhoons causing flooding 
in the complex areas, FPC strengthens 
the inspection, repair, and maintenance of 
drainage ditches, sluice gates, and pumping 
equipment. In 2022, we invested a total 
of NT$1,622,000 in response measures, 
strengthened the alert mechanism for 
water level monitoring, and established an 
emergency response plan.
1. There are a total of 17 flood control pumps 
in the Renwu and Linyuan Complexes, 
providing a pumping capacity of 49,390 M
3/
hour to reduce the probability of flooding in 
the factory area caused by heavy rainfall.
2. The Mailiao Complex carries out large-scale 
sand discharge and dredging operations 
annually to reduce the probability of flooding 
in the plant area caused by heavy rainfall.
1. The Linyuan Complex has drilled 2 drought-
resistant wells, which can increase water 
supply by 2,300 M
3/day, and the investment 
cost is NT$4,428 thousand.
2. Cooperate with the public sector to source 
the underflow water of Donggang River and 
Gaoping River to stabilize the water supply. 
In addition, we will evaluate and develop 
wastewater treatment for high ammonia 
nitrogen in the Huliao River, and then exchange 
water for water to obtain water rights.
3. In response to the potential risk of plant 
shutdown due to water shortage or drought, 
FPC has dug drought-resistant wells, and the 
investment cost is NT$7,428 thousand.
4. A 100,000 tons/day seawater desalination plant is 
planned to start running in 2023, which will reduce 
the external water supply demand by 40%.
5. Taking 2% of the total water consumption 
in 2022 as the base level of water scarcity, 
in order to secure additional water supply 
from other sources, a basic contract fee of 
NT$100,000 will incur, with NT$10,000 per 
30 M
3 of water and NT$12 per M
3 of water. 
The total expenditure is estimated to be 
NT$237,860,000.

Climate Change Mitigation and Adaptation Strategy
In order to mitigate climate change, FPC has formulated short-, medium- and long-term response 
strategies for the period after 2021. In the future, we will achieve the goal of progressive carbon reduction 
through the transformation of coal burning to low (zero) carbon energy, energy-saving and carbon-
reducing circular economy, increasing the use of renewable energy, and other carbon reduction measures.

3.2.2 Greenhouse Gases Management
2-25 3-3 305-1 305-2 
305-3 305-4
Management policy
Material Topic:
Greenhouse Gases Management
International 
Sustainability 
Frameworks
GRI 305-1 305-2 305-3 305-4
SASB: Greenhouse Gas Emissions
MSCI: Carbon Emissions
Policy 
Commitments
Promote carbon neutral strategies and set GHG reduction targets with 2020 
as the base year: “20% reduction in 2025 compared with the base year, 40% 
reduction in 2030 compared with the base year, and achievement of carbon 
neutrality by 2050”. Specific strategies include: transformation of coal burning to 
low (zero) carbon energy, energy-saving and carbon-reducing circular economy, 
increasing use of renewable energy, and other carbon reduction measures (such 
as developing carbon capture technology).
Management 
Approach and 
Performance 
Monitoring
Promote internal carbon pricing, set annual carbon reduction targets for 
each complex, and include carbon costs in the profit and loss statement of 
each complex, so as to examine greenhouse gas emissions and future carbon 
reduction plans on a monthly basis and to implement carbon reduction targets
According to our policy commitments, each complex establishes annual carbon 
reduction goals and calculates the amount of carbon emissions and the target 
achievement rate on a monthly basis to monitor our carbon footprint. For any 
complex that fails to meet the monthly control standard, an explanation and 
future carbon reduction plan must be submitted to each business division and the 
President's Office for further monitoring and management. 
Stakeholder 
Engagement
Stakeholders: Shareholders and Investors, Experts, Scholars, and 
Environmental Protection Organizations, Customers, Suppliers 
and Contractors
Contact details, including phone number and e-mail address, are provided in 
the "Investor Relations" section on FPC's official website, so that stakeholders 
can have access to channels of communication with FPC.
In order to fulfill our corporate responsibility and to meet the requirements of future greenhouse 
gas reduction, FPC has set up and maintained a systematic inventory of GHG emissions since 2006 in 
accordance with ISO 14064-1:2006. Furthermore, the British Standards Institution (BSI) and SGS Taiwan are 
commissioned to conduct Scope 1 and Scope 2 emissions. The inventory scope has been expanded to cover 
Scope 3 emissions since 2016, and SGS has been entrusted to complete the verification since 2020. Three 
items in the areas of upstream and downstream leased assets, chain/licensed distribution and investments 
were not checked for these 4 categories because they were less relevant to the Company's business.
Official Website: Stakeholder Services

90
2022 Formosa Plastics Corporation　Sustainability Report
In addition, to increase awareness of greenhouse gas emissions and strengthen the implementation 
of carbon reduction efforts at each complex, we have implemented internal carbon pricing (ICP) in 
2022. Through our self-developed greenhouse gas calculation system, costs of greenhouse gas carbon 
emissions (including excess carbon emission costs) are incorporated into our business performance 
assessment every month, so as to accelerate the reduction of greenhouse gases at each complex. 
Meanwhile, to promote carbon reduction in the supply chain, the "equipment selection analysis table" 
for procurement projects of high-carbon emission equipment is used by the procurement departments 
to estimate equipment carbon emissions and to incorporate carbon emission costs into procurement 
selection process.
In 2021, the inventory of GHG Scope 1 emissions was 3,918,988 tons of CO2e, Scope 1 emissions was 
4,685,085 tons of CO2e, and Scope 3 emissions was 10,445,602 tons of CO2e, totaling 19,049,675 tons of 
CO2e. The percentages of Scope 1 and Scope 2 emissions of each complex are shown below.

FPC Carbon Reduction Implementation Plans
Plan: Renewable Energy - Solar Panels at Renwu Complex
Description
FPC invested NT$43.87 million in building two sets of solar power systems with a total of 1,669 solar panels 
on the rooftops of the welfare building and the parking building, respectively, at the Renwu Complex.
Annual Results and Future Plans
1. FPC has installed its own solar power generation capacity, with 456 kW already completed so far. 
The total power generation in 2022 was 518,359 kW. As it was entirely sold to Taipower, it is not 
included in our carbon reduction calculation.
2. FPC will continue to increase renewable energy through the following measures:
a. We will keep looking for suitable locations where renewable energy can be developed and expand 
our solar power generation systems for self-use. Currently, the estimated installation capacity 
of each complex is about 4,000 kW, with an annual power generation of 5.296 million kWh and an 
annual carbon reduction of 4,443 tons.
b. Purchase of wind power, solar renewable energy, and green power certificates from Formosa 
Heavy Industries Corporation.
c. Purchase green electricity certificates from green energy trading platform operators.
3. 2025 Target: 100% of all administrative areas in all complexes will use renewable energy.
Plan: Promote Product Carbon Footprint Inventory
Description
FPC has not only set carbon reduction 
targets, but also obtained product 
lifecycle assessment certificates 
(including carbon footprint inventory) 
from TUV Rheinland since 2019, and 
completed carbon footprint inventory 
for major products in 2022. Through 
the carbon footprint inventory, we 
hope to understand the carbon dioxide 
emissions generated directly (indirectly) 
during the life cycle of our products, 
so that our customers can grasp the 
carbon footprint of their end products 
and apply for carbon footprint labels.
Annual Results and Future Plans
FPC has applied for carbon footprint 
verification for a total of 72 products. 
As of the end of 2022, a total of 
54 products obtained the Carbon 
Footprint Verification Opinion 
Statement. We will continue to work 
on greenhouse gas reduction and 
product carbon footprint reduction.

Appendix
3.3.2 Water Usage 
FPC sources water from surface water (rainwater, river water, and tap water) and groundwater, and 
uses it in production as raw materials or solvents, cooling water for equipment during the process, and 
domestic water at complexes.
In response to the government's environmental policy, each complex continues to implement circular 
economy by reducing water consumption or reusing water resources, or taking other measures such as 
improving the steam piping system to reduce wastewater, installing rainwater storage tanks to increase 
the amount of rainwater collected, improving the cooling system to reduce evaporation, and recycling 
cooling water to reuse wastewater. We are committed to reusing precious water resources when possible. 
At the Mailiao Park, a drop of water was used 7.3 times in 2015. After years of continuous promotion, a 
drop of water could be used 12.7 times in 2021.
Water Resources Management Measures
Reduce demand for water resources, 
enhance reuse of water resources, and 
accelerate the recycling treatment process
Implement waste reduction during 
production processes to reduce load on 
treatment facilities
After the water resources that cannot be 
reused are detoxified by the treatment 
facilities, the end-of-pipe method is used 
to determine the discharge in compliance 
with regulations and standards, and the 
environmental impact is minimized.
Hold water and energy 
conservation meetings 
every month to review the 
performance of water 
and energy conservation 
at each complex

of water consumption and

Appendix
3.3.3 Improvements in Water 
Conservation Performance
The water sources used in the FPC's complexes mainly consist of surface water and groundwater. Under 
the condition of limited water resources, FPC not only implements various improvement measures, such as 
reducing water use in production processes, engaging in water conservation, and reducing evaporation loss, 
but also requires all departments to set annual targets for unit water consumption based on the principle that 
the water consumption target for a particular year should be 5% less than the average in the previous year. 
1. If the department's water consumption rate of the previous year is equal to or more than 100%, the 
annual target should be the department's net consumption of the previous year × 95%.
2. If the department's water consumption rate of the previous year is less than 95%, the annual target 
should be the department's net consumption of the previous year.
3. 95% ≦ Achievement rate of unit water consumption in the previous year ＜ 100%, the annual target 
should be the department's net consumption of the previous year × 95% or the target of 2021, 
whichever is lower.

To improve water efficiency, Mailiao Complex has long 
been strengthening rainwater harvesting. Rainwater is 
effectively stored and reused through various methods 
such as increasing the rainwater collection surface area 
and modifying rainwater storage tank pipelines. The total 
rainwater recovery in 2022 was 4,442 tons per day, and 
the total rainwater recovery rate was 81%. For the Mailiao 
complex particularly, in 2022, its rainwater recycling 
amount was 3,175 tons/day, and its rainwater recycling rate 
was 127%. Compared with the average rainwater recycling 
amount of 3,566 tons/day and rainwater recycling rate 
of 118% from 2019 to 2021, the rainwater recycling rate 
reduced by 391 tons/day, while the rainwater recovery rate 
increased by 9%. For more information about the amount

3.3.4 Zero Wastewater Discharge
To progress toward the ideal goal of zero wastewater discharge, the President's Office is tasked to 
promote the development of wastewater treatment technologies company-wide and assist each complex 
in improving internal wastewater treatment technologies.
For example, the Renwu Complex is expected to invest NT$1.2 billion in the zero wastewater discharge 
plan, which is divided into four stages, namely, source reduction, cooling water recycling, effluent 
recycling, and zero discharge of concentrated wastewater, to achieve the goal of zero wastewater 
discharge. The situation at each stage is described as follows:
303-1 303-2
Implementation
Results in 2022
Source reduction
Strengthen the source control of 
production wastewater discharge, 
such as: improve the production 
process, reduce the amount of water 
used, reduce abnormal, mass, or 
highly-concentrated wastewater into 
wastewater treatment facilities, reuse 
waste water, etc., to reduce wastewater 
discharge
1. There were a total of 28 improvement plans for 
source reduction of wastewater, 26 of which 
have been completed. Due to consideration of 
product quality and the biological wastewater 
treatment system, after careful review, 
the remaining 2 improvement plans will be 
canceled and replaced by other more feasible 
reduction solutions.
2. Taking Renwu alkali plant as an example, 
the recovery of acidic wastewater from the 
resin tower and the improvement of the brine 
filtration system are being evaluated and 
planned. It is estimated that the amount of 
wastewater can be reduced by 0.226 million 
liters per day.
Cooling water 
recycling
Cooling tower is the main source of 
water discharge. For recycling of water 
discharge from cooling towers at the 
Renwu Complex, UF/RO membranes 
are prone to clogging due to water 
quality characteristics. Therefore, FPC 
developed a patent that enables water 
quality to meet the UF/RO water quality 
standards upon pre-treatment.
In 2022, FPC tried to recycle water discharged 
from cooling towers with self-developed 
patents. However, due to the excessive increase 
in the amount of wastewater sludge, it was 
not successful. In order to confirm the right 
proportion of recycling and deployment, we are 
planning to conduct more tests to establish 
further wastewater recycling plans.
Efﬂuent recycling
It is divided into three stages, namely 
(1) laboratory test, (2) simulated field 
test, and (3) physical construction. Due 
to the characteristics of water quality, 
it is difficult to recycle and easily cause 
RO membrane blockage. Laboratory 
test is currently in progress to analyze 
the water quality of effluent, test dosing 
bottles and cups, test coagulation 
and sedimentation, discharge water 
recovery, and the standard test 
of reprocessing the concentrated 
drainage to discharge water etc., so 
as to facilitate subsequent planning of 
wastewater treatment and recycling 
units as well as the implementation of 
simulated field test in the second stage.
As the process wastewater of the Renwu carbon 
fiber plant contains ammonia nitrogen, it is 
treated by traditional methods, such as heating 
stripping, biological aeration, and break point 
chlorination, which consumes more energy and 
is less efficient. Therefore, we have implemented 
a plan to improve the biological system at 
the wastewater treatment plant. In 2022, the 
integrated treatment of anaerobic/anaerobic/
aerobic organisms has been implemented to test 
the results. It was estimated that the wastewater 
volume could be reduced by 0.34 million liters/
day, and the steam energy consumption could be 
reduced by about 75.2 GJ/day (25 tons/day). The 
test results were very positive. In 2023, we will 
start conducting simulated field tests.
Zero discharge 
of concentrated 
wastewater
FPC continues to assess concentrated 
wastewater discharged from RO as well 
as re-concentrate, recycle, and reuse 
concentrated wastewater, so as to 
achieve the goal of zero discharge.
After the testing of the effluent recycling 
technology is completed, we will then establish 
plans for the recovery and reuse of highly 
concentrated wastewater.

Appendix
 
  Water Pollution Prevention Measures  
To maximize the effect of water pollution prevention, it is necessary to classify wastewater for 
management from the source. For instance, the Renwu Complex has 6 wastewater treatment plants in 
place for organic and inorganic wastewater treatment to deal with different types of wastewater, and 
has also set up 5 monitoring systems to connect with local authorities in real time. The water quality 
monitoring results have been better than the statutory standards.
In line with the Kaohsiung City Government's policy to build the Houjing River Park, FPC has invested 
NT$110 million in building 4.8 km of sea discharge pipelines in 2019 to discharge all sources of discharge 
at the Renda Industrial Park into the sea. The sea discharge pipelines from the Renwu complex to the 
Nanzih pumping station are long-distance submersible pipelines with high pressure which limits waste 
water discharge into the sea.
The sea discharge rate of the Renwu complex in 2022 was 95.2%, and the improvement and reconstruction 
of the wastewater treatment plant is continuously being made, so as to divert waste water to the Nanzih 
and Dashe pumping stations and to reduce the pressure of the sea discharge pipelines. Except for heavy 
rain and maintenance of the equipment and pipelines at the Nanzih sea discharge center, since January 
2023, all waste water has been discharged to the sea (zero river discharge).

Appendix
3.4.1 Air Pollution Monitoring and Assessment
(1) Air quality
To keep abreast of various environmental indicators in real time at Mailiao Complex, FPC sets out to 
establish a comprehensive environmental monitoring network comprising eight layers of intensive 
monitoring control by referencing local prevailing wind directions. This allows us to track emission 
sources in real-time, thereby ensuring the air quality around the complex areas. For more information on 
air pollution management and prevention, please refer to our Sustainable Development website. 
(2) Air quality impact analysis
To monitor the air quality, FPC purchased 6 sets of 
Fourier-transform infrared spectroscopy (FTIR), three 
of which were stationed at Mailiao, Renwu, and Linyuan 
Complexes; the other three sets are mobile, which can 
effectively and immediately detect air quality anomalies 
for improvement at the complexes. 
Fixed FTIR Station
Mobile FTIR (e.g., turnaround and anomaly detection)
3.4.2 Air Pollution Control Measures
FPC strives to reduce air pollution by adopting the best available technology and air pollution control 
equipment, and appointing two employees (one of them being the substitute staff) which is better than the 
statutory requirements, to be in charge of air pollution control at each unit. Air pollution control personnel 
are required to pass national examinations to ensure the effectiveness of air pollution control measures at 
each complex. At present, FPC's pollution control results have surpassed national standards and are on a 
par with the performance of global optimization standards.
Our 2025 reduction targets for various air pollutants will be reduced by 5% compared with 2020, and we 
will achieve the best feasible control efficiency for air pollution control in our manufacturing processes. 
These reduction targets will be achieved by adding additional pollution prevention equipment, improving the 
efficiency of the prevention equipment, and by tightening regulations and voluntary reduction of air pollutants.

Improvements in Exhaust Emissions
Replacement of pollution prevention equipment at the Renwu 
caustic soda plant (Waste liquid and waste gas incinerator)
Additional installation of pollution prevention equipment at the

Additional 
installation of 
pollution prevention 
equipment
In order to improve the exhaust gas 
emission, a regenerative incinerator 
was added at the end of the process to 
reduce the output of VOCs.
The regenerative incinerator newly installed 
at the Renwu carbon fiber plant has obtained 
the operating permit from the Kaohsiung City 
Environmental Protection Bureau in November 
2022 and has been officially placed into operation 
for waste gas treatment to increase the waste 
gas treatment efficiency from 95% to 98% as 
compared with the catalytic oxidation furnace.
Improve the 
efﬁciency of control 
equipment
The Mailiao MMA plant replaced the 
catalyst of the sulfuric acid catalytic 
converter with a high-efficiency 
catalyst to improve the conversion rate 
of sulfur dioxide, so as to facilitate the 
reaction to generate sulfuric acid and 
reduce the emission of sulfur oxides.
Since 2019, FPC has started the replacement 
with high-efficiency catalysts, which was fully 
completed in 2022, and the concentration of 
sulfur oxides can be reduced to below 220 ppm.
Tightening of 
regulations
In line with the stringent standards 
for air pollutant emissions from 
power facilities in Kaohsiung City, the 
SOx standard in the first stage was 
reduced from 50 ppm to 25 ppm; the 
NOx standard was reduced from 80 
ppm to 50 ppm.
SCR catalysts and desulfurization agents have 
been introduced at the Renwu and Linyuan public 
utilities complexes. As of the end of December 
2022, the concentration of SOx and NOx 
emissions was successfully reduced to below the 
stringent standards.
Voluntary reduction 
of air pollutants
In addition to ensuring that various 
pollutants comply with environmental 
protection regulations, FPC also 
continues to promote air pollution 
reduction projects.
Streamlining of the components of petrochemical 
process equipment to streamline pipelines and 
reduce the number of equipment components, 
thereby lowering the emissions of volatile organic 
compounds from equipment components.
In 2022, 21,664 units were streamlined, reducing 
VOCs emissions by 2.734 tons/year as well as 
saving costs of NT$1,309 thousand/year (including 
inspection fees of NT$1,213 thousand/year and 
air pollution fees of NT$96 thousand/year).
Improvement in 
visual pollution
A medium gas-gas heater (MGGH) is 
used for heating tail gas of a chimney 
to eliminate white smoke and reduce 
PM2.5 emissions.
Improvements of all six cogeneration units owned 
by FPC have been completed at the end of April, 
2022.

3.5 Waste Management  
3.5.1 Waste Impact Identification
FPC carries out waste reduction through three major measures, including source management, process 
reduction and end-of-pipe disposal, so the waste directly disposed of is the actual waste. In addition, we 
are committed to promoting the reuse of waste and reducing the amount of landfills.
In order to reduce the amount of direct waste disposal, a target of 10% reduction in direct disposal in 2025 
compared to 2020 (base year) and 20% reduction in 2030 compared to the base year has been set. In 2022, 
the waste directly disposed of by FPC was 27,509 tons, a slight increase from 27,457 tons in 2021. We will 
continue to improve.
306-1 306-2 306-3 306-4 306-5

Self-operation
Downstream
If the supply of upstream raw 
materials is of poor quality, 
FPC will need to spend more 
energy resources which 
generates more waste. 
Excessive waste may exceed 
the permitted amount for 
environmental protection, 
and production needs to be 
reduced in severe cases.
The poor quality of upstream 
raw material supply causes 
FPC to spend more energy 
(resources) to purify the raw 
materials, resulting in excess 
waste.
Actual or potential impact
Causes
If there is an increase in the 
amount of waste or 
abnormal quality, the waste 
treatment or recycling 
industry cannot process or 
reuse it. In severe cases, it 
may be necessary to reduce 
(or stop) production in order 
to reduce (or stop) the 
production of waste.
Actual or potential impact
When there is an 
abnormality in the process 
operation, the waste 
produced by the process 
will increase or will cause 
abnormality in the quality.
Causes

unable to accept waste due to

FPC’s Waste Management System
Results in 2022
Processing Method
1. The waste materials generated during production stages, 
such as the by-products (previously disposed of as waste) 
derived from the production process of U-CAL, were 
recycled and reused to produce low-end products (TAICAL), 
with a waste reduction of 14.4 tons.
2. The biological sludge produced by the waste water treatment 
site at the Renwu complex was too high in water content, 
and occasionally due to the poor heat treatment efficiency of 
the waste treatment site, it could not be accepted for 
treatment. In 2022, additional steam drying equipment was 
installed to reduce the moisture content of sludge from 80% 
to 30%, which would reduce the output of biochemical sludge 
by 500 tons per month.
For pipelines or equipment with low thermal insulation 
requirements in the process, they are replaced by spraying 
thermal insulation paint to reduce the waste of thermal 
insulation or cold insulation materials during maintenance of 
pipelines or equipment.
Process improvement to 
reduce output and reuse 
process materials
1. FPC worked with cement product companies to submit an 
application to the Industrial Development Bureau of the 
Ministry of Economic Affairs to reuse industrial waste 
(calcium fluoride sludge) as cement product additives, and 
the application was approved in February 2022. Previously, 
the sludge waste needed to be disposed of by heat 
treatment, but it was then reused as cement product 
additives, reducing total waste by 150 tons per month.
2. FPC has worked with waste treatment companies to 
submit an application to the Ministry of Economic Affairs to 
reuse inorganic sludge. FPC has submitted an application 
to the Industrial Development Bureau of the Ministry of 
Economic Affairs in November 2022, and if approved, about 
2,000 tons of waste can be reduced per month.
Selling the by-product 
and recycle waste

3.6 Management of Hazardous Substances
3.6.1 Hazardous Substance Management Measures
 
Hazardous Substance Management Strategy
Through chemical selection, assessment of chemical safety and product hazard, FPC reduces the harmful 
substances used in the production process and in products to protect the health of employees and consumers.
Management

Dimethylformamide (DMF) originally used 
at the Renwu carbon fiber plant is a toxic 
chemical substance regulated by the 
Environmental Protection Administration 
and is a widely used solvent in the 
manufacturing process. After process 
development and improvement, DMF was 
replaced by the non-toxic solvent dimethyl 
sulfoxide (DMSO).

1. FPC classifies the chemicals that are 
produced, disposed of, or used by its 
workers according to the national 
standards. For those with health hazards, 
FPC evaluates the hazards and exposure 
levels, identifies the risk levels, and take 
corresponding management measures.
2. Each complex has employed professional 
and technical management personnel 
(holding valid licenses) and completed 
the on-the-job training for a total of 26 
professional and technical management 
personnel to help improve the learning 
ability of management personnel.
3. We have strengthened our management 
mechanism of the detection and 
alarm system to ensure that all data 
abnormalities are verified and corrected.
Product 
Hazard

 Hazard assessment for all

1. FPC has established chemical substance 
hazard data and implemented process 
hazard assessment technology for all 
chemicals (including raw materials 
and products) used at the complexes in 
accordance with FPC’s process safety 
management policies. Major potential 
hazards related to the process or 
disposal of highly hazardous chemical 
substances are identified and analyzed in 
an organized and systematic way.
2.Taking PVC products as an example, 
we independently controls the VCM 
(a hazardous substance) in PVC to be 
less than 1 ppm to reduce the risk 
of exposure to harmful substances 
during transportation and downstream 
customer processing.

110
2022 Formosa Plastics Corporation　Sustainability Report
 
Hazardous Chemical Safety
To manage hazardous substances at each complex (including EPA's 
controlled chemical substances and hazardous chemical substances), 
FPC strictly requires that all management personnel obtain professional 
and technical licenses and that all complexes are equipped with detection 
and alarm systems. Related products are subject to hazard assessment 
according to law, and unused EPA's controlled chemical substances are 
managed as hazardous industrial waste and properly treated after being 
declared as waste in accordance with the law.
In 2022, FPC worked with 7 qualified waste disposal contractors and 5 
treatment contractors and conducted inspections and visits on an irregular 
basis to ensure that hazardous industrial waste was properly treated.
For EPA's controlled chemical substances and toxic chemicals, FPC has 
appointed more professional technical management personnel and emergency response personnel (holding 
valid licenses) than the statutory requirements at each complex. FPC has also completed the on-the-job 
training for all such personnel to help improve the learning ability of management personnel.

According to the “Regulations of New and Existing Chemical Substances Registration” , standard 
registration should be carried out on 106 chemical substances, where information such as manufacturing 
or import situation, category and labeling, and toxicology and ecotoxicity has to be registered on EPA's 
Chemical Substances Register. We have completed the registration of acrylic acid in 2022, along with other 
businesses in the industry, and the registration of other substances is still being processed.
3.6.2 Development of Alternatives
In response to the global sustainability initiatives, FPC has reduced the environmental cost of its products. 
Since 2019, it has adopted three strategies, namely "sustainability", "prevention", and "assurance", 
and gradually developed alternatives that are less harmful to the human body and the environment. 
FPC continues to enhance the safety of chemicals and chemical reaction processes in order to replace 
the use of hazardous substances or to eliminate or reduce the impact of hazardous substances on the 
environment as much as possible.
 
Case Example
Originally, the ODS refrigerant such as CFC-11/12/22 
was in use, after the improvement of the process, 
the freezing temperature of the process is being 
adjusted and the refrigerant material to non-toxic 
propylene, R134a and other low-hazard refrigerants 
are adopted.
Turn off the processes with nitrogen trifluoride (NF3) 
NF3 is a cleaning and etching gas commonly used 
in semiconductor manufacturing processes. It has 
high oxidation properties and is a greenhouse gas 
17,000 times stronger than carbon dioxide. In order 
to reduce carbon emissions, we have shut down 
the nitrogen trifluoride process in 2017 to reduce 
the greenhouse effect caused by the leakage of NF3 
during the production process.
Low-hazard refrigerant
Turn off the processes with high greenhouse gas
Removal of NF3 pipelines and equipment
If the original catalyst solvent is heptane (a 
dangerous article), replace it with low-hazard 
white oil (mineral oil).
Adjust the catalyst solvent in the process
Before removal
After removal

4.1 Employee Profile
4.1.1 Manpower Structure
FPC had a total of 6,379 employees in 2022 who were all full-time employees, of whom 6,196 were 
permanent employees, accounting for 97.1% of the total number of employees, and 183 (approximately 
2.9%) were temporary employees such as consultants, contract employees, and part-time students 
workers. Due to the characteristics of the industries to which FPC belongs, the ratio of male to female 
employees is approximately 9.1:1. Meanwhile, the average age of employees is 44.0 years old, while the 
average length of service is 17.98 years. Our employees are mostly in the 40 to 49 years old age group, 
indicating that our colleagues put their trust in FPC and have developed a sense of belonging at FPC.

Note 1: Permanent employee: employee with a contract for an indeterminate period (i.e., indefinite contract) for full-time or part-time work
Note 2: Temporary employee: employee with a contract for a limited period (i.e., fixed term contract). The contract ends when the specific time period expires, 
or when the specific task or event that has an attached time estimate is completed (e.g., the end of a project or return of replaced employees).
Note 3: Full-time employee: employee whose working hours per week, month, or year are defined according to national law or practice regarding working time
Note 4: Part-time employee: employee whose working hours per week, month, or year are less than the number of working hours for full-time employees
Note 5: Non-guaranteed hours employee: employee who is not guaranteed a minimum or fixed number of working hours per day, week, or month, but who 
may need to make themselves available for work as required
In 2022, a total of 262 regular employees resigned from FPC, including 70 employees (26.7%) who retired 
early and 49 employees (18.7%) who officially retired. Over the past four years, the annual employee 
turnover rate has remained below 4.2%, and the overall turnover rate after deducting all retirees has been 
about 3.1%. For more details, please refer to Appendix I: ESG Key Performance.

violations of human rights or discrimination in 2022 was zero. For the description of FPC's diversified 
composition of employees and performance results, please refer to the following table:

FPC not only employs more people with

and proportion of female supervisors

Talent Recruitment Channels
In order to actively recruit diverse talents to enhance FPC's workforce, we take the initiative in sending 
invitations to new graduates from public and private colleges and universities to apply for the jobs we have 
available through campus recruitments, job banks, and other channels. Meanwhile, job vacancies are 
simultaneously announced at FPC and posted on our official talent recruitment website. In 2022, due to the 
COVID-19 pandemic prevention policy, most interviews were conducted via video conference.
FPC Talent Recruitment Website
In order to increase exposure and diversify talent recruitment 
channels, FPC has set up a talent recruitment website to 
provide easily accessible information about job opportunities 
and requirements. Talents who are interested in FPC and have 
great ambitions are welcome to apply and join us to create a 
better future together.

4.2 Compensation, Benefits and Training
4.2.1 Compensation and Benefits
In order to attract outstanding talents from different sectors, FPC provides competitive remuneration 
packages. The salary of employees includes basic salary, efficiency bonus, various allowances, three-festival 
bonus and supervisor bonus, etc. According to operational performance and personal performance, year-
end bonuses ranging from 3 to 7 months will be issued 
every year, and labor insurance, health insurance, 
and pension (including 6% of the new system) are 
paid according to the law and regulations. The actual 
employment cost in 2022 was NT$ 1,629.1 thousand per 
person on average, and the total employment cost was 
over NT$10 billion.

To implement the concept of a happy workplace, FPC has not only established breastfeeding rooms at each 
complex, but also promoted the unpaid parental leave program to provide parental leave, enabling the 
eligible employees to apply based on their needs. These measures are not only a part of fulfilling corporate 
social responsibility, but also fulfilling our commitment to employee happiness and family harmony. We 
firmly believe that through such measures, employees can better balance work and life, thereby enhancing 
company performance and value.
In 2022, 6 employees applied for unpaid parental leave and 3 employees were actually reinstated in the 
year (the other 3 employees are still on parental leave without pay), indicating a reinstatement rate of 50%. 
In addition, 7 employees were reinstated in 2021, with all of them remaining at FPC for more than one year, 
representing a 100% retention rate. For more details, please refer to Appendix I: ESG Key Performance.
In addition, in order to encourage employees to have children, FPC 
has started offering incentives for childbirth since July 2022, including 
delicate lucky gift bags for employees or their spouses who are pregnant 
or giving birth, a cash gift of NT$20,000 for each newborn, and a monthly 
childcare allowance of NT$2,000 for each baby until the age of 6, so as to 
express blessings and support for new life.
In 2022, a total of 58 FPC babies benefited from the incentive program, 
with a total of NT$1,160 thousand in childbirth cash gifts. Also, 864 
employees applied for childcare subsidies, with a total of NT$13,004 
thousand issued. We hope that these incentives can further improve the 
happiness and productivity of employees as well as make meaningful 
contributions to society.
4.2.2 Training and Performance Management
The scope of performance evaluation includes all regular employees. Individual employee performance is 
regularly assessed every month, which is then used as the benchmark for efficiency bonus. On the other 
hand, the evaluation results are compiled at the end of the year as a reference for managers to carry out 
year-end performance evaluation of employees in order to ensure the objectivity of such evaluation. In 
2022, the proportion of employees of all genders and ranks in the company's regular evaluation was 100%. 
For more details, please refer to Appendix I: ESG Key Performance.
Employees with outstanding performance are not only provided with opportunities and channels for 
promotion and salary increment, but also awarded year-end bonuses based on the business performance 
and individual employee performance evaluation. Through the aforementioned performance management 
and encouragement, FPC closely links employee performance and company goals, creating a win-win 
situation for both FPC and employees.
FPC has developed a set of comprehensive training programs and recorded relevant training data through the 
electronic training platform in order to implement the objective of providing all-round training for employees.

to improve operating performance. FPC has assigned employees to

since 2018, so as to keep abreast of the latest trends and applications 
as well as cultivate AI talents. After the COVID-19 pandemic gradually

resume various trainings. Therefore, the overall training hours increased 
significantly compared with 2021.

4.2.3 Employee Communication and Care
FPC complies with the provisions of the Labor Standards Act and other relevant laws and regulations 
to implement a complete notification procedure and ensure that employees understand their rights 
and interests in advance. Moreover, we are committed to providing 
multiple channels of communication, encouraging employees to actively 
propose innovative ideas, and strengthening communication between 
employees and management. Employees can make suggestions for 
better working or living conditions to FPC through organizations such 
as welfare committees, labor-management meetings, labor unions, and 
occupational safety and health committees, as well as report problems 
through complaint channels.
A total of 4,739 employees at FPC have joined labor unions as of 2022. 
Even if regular employees do not join a labor union, their rights such 
as salary adjustments and year-end bonuses are protected by the 
agreement signed between FPC and the employees.
We are well aware of the importance of employee work experience and 
skills in the development of a company. Therefore, through regular care 
and consultation provided by our employee counselors, we ensure that 
newly recruited management associates or personnel who are under 
special conditions can adapt to the working environment promptly, 
understand the company culture, and be familiar with job requirements. 
At the same time, we also help employees overcome work and life 
related difficulties in order to improve job satisfaction, increase 
employee loyalty, and reduce employee turnover. We believe that these 
measures will help establish a healthy, stable, and efficient working 
environment as well as further enhance trust and communication 
between employees and FPC.
 
  Human Rights Management
FPC never uses forced labor and prohibits child labor or illegal labor. In 2022, there were no incidents 
of discrimination based on the race, gender, religion, political party, or sexual orientation, sexual 
harassment, or bullying in the workplace at FPC. In addition, Chairman Jason Lin signed the new human 
rights policy in August 2019 and signed FPC’s Diversity and Inclusion Policy and Modern Slavery Statement 
in March 2023.  
Diversity and Inclusion Policy
FPC firmly believes in the value of diverse and inclusive workplaces, respects diverse differences, and 
ensures that equal opportunities are provided to all employees regardless of race, nationality, age, gender, 
sexual orientation, marriage status, political affiliation, religion, blood type, zodiac sign, and so forth in an 
effort to create an environment where diverse talents can thrive.
Furthermore, we will continue to consider the current social situation, commit to promoting diversity and 
inclusion, strengthen multifaceted management and employee profile, as well as support and respond 
appropriately to different perspectives, values, and needs, so as to enhance our competitive advantage.

Modern Slavery Statement
FPC is committed to combating all forms of modern slavery. In addition to promising not to force 
employees to work or participate in any other activities, FPC does not impose any restrictions on freedom 
or any form of exploitation. We comply with the local labor laws and regulations at all operating locations to 
ensure employee rights and proper working conditions as well as strive to create a working environment 
that satisfies and respects employees.
We provide equal employment opportunities and firmly oppose 
discrimination, harassment, and unfair treatment. At the same time, we 
also respect employee privacy and freedom of association. Additionally, 
FPC has implemented a number of measures to ensure that all suppliers 
and contractors comply with modern slavery statement requirements.
We believe that only when employees are treated with respect and fairness 
can they realize their full potential and make valuable contributions to 
the company. Therefore, we regularly collect opinions and feedback from 
employees to understand their needs and views and take measures to 
improve the working environment and welfare benefits to the best we can.

Employee Care
Teacher Chang Foundation
In order to improve the mental health and happiness of employees, 
we collaborate with the Teacher Chang Foundation to arrange for 
professional counselors to come to the complexes and provide 
consultations. Employees can make appointments and have one-
on-one consultations on the e-interview appointment platform of 
the "FPC Mobile" app according to their needs, which enhances 
the psychological care of employees and protects their privacy. A 
total of 59 interviews were completed in 2022, which was positively 
received by employees for three consecutive years. We will 
continue to improve and optimize the existing counseling program 
according to the needs and feedback of employees. 
 
Employee Retirement Plan
In addition to the labor pension and labor insurance old-age benefits, FPC or the employee welfare 
committee will also award employees with incentives or medals according to their positions to express 
thanks for their contributions over the years. For more information on retirement measures, please refer 
to our website.
In order to appreciate retired employees' contributions to the company, "FPG Retirement Association" 
was established in 2013, including six branches in Taipei, Yilan, Beitao, Changhua, Chiayi and Kaohsiung, 
providing retired employees with a platform to participate in leisure activities, communication and making 
friends to enrich their lives.
In addition to networking activities, retired employees can also become corporate policy advocates, 
corporate image defenders, and participants in corporate social responsibility feedback to enhance 
corporate image. According to statistics in 2022, a total of 704 retired employees participated, with a total 
annual allocation of NT$704,000 (NT$1,000 per person per year).

4.3 Workplace Safety Management
4.3.1 Occupational Health and Safety
International 
Sustainability 
Frameworks
GRI: 403-1 403-2 403-3 403-4 403-5 403-6 403-7 403-8 403-9 403-10
SASB: Workforce Health & Safety
Policy 
Commitments
Committed to establishing a people-oriented safe and healthy workplace, prevent 
occupational disasters, ensure the safety and health of workers, prevent unsafe actions 
and behaviors of personnel, and strengthen inspection and inspection of machinery and 
equipment to reduce the frequency-severity indicator by 20% every year, with “Zero 
Disaster” as the ultimate goal.
 
◈Building safe equipment and facilities.
 
◈Plan and implement regular and key inspections of machinery and equipment, 
operational inspections, and on-site inspections.
 
◈All employees and contractors participate in education and training, standard 
operating procedures (SOP, including safety operation standards) and Safety 
Walking and Talking (SWAT) to reduce the chance of human error.
 
◈Promote total inspection in each complex and office, and conduct in-depth 
inspection and discovery of potential risks not identified in the operational 
procedures, including safety, health, process, SOP, machinery, electrical 
equipment and inspection.
 
◈Introducing AI technology for confined space image recognition and smart 
glasses/watches and other wearable devices to assist in safety management 
and maintenance to protect personnel and equipment safety.
 
◈Promote occupational safety and health management regulations and plans, 
and enhance the management (including risk assessment) of process safety 
events (PSE) and near-misses.
 
◈Promote chemical exposure assessment and health classification management 
among employees.

◈In 2022, a total of 174 occupational safety education and training sessions for 
contractors were held, with 5,312 attendees.

◈Arrange occupational physicians and nurses to provide on-site consultation 
services for employees with abnormal health check results.
 
◈In 2022, a total of 1,571 employees received health guidance, and 26 health 
seminars were held, with a total of 2,372 participating employees.

124
2022 Formosa Plastics Corporation　Sustainability Report
FPC has set up an organizational structure with division of responsibilities and powers and established 
occupational safety and health management system according to law. Meanwhile, FPC also promotes 
occupational health and safety management through formulating safety and health objectives, 
management regulations and plans, process safety management implementation, and employee health 
care services as well as using a risk-based approach, in an effort to provide a healthy and safe working 
environment for all factory employees.
To this end, all complexes have passed the ISO 45001 and CNS 45001 Occupational Safety and Health 
Management System Certification in 2022. In 2023, we will also continue to perform regular follow-up 
inspections of the occupational safety and health management system to ensure the effectiveness and 
continuous improvement of our management system.
The workers defined by the Occupational Safety and Health Management System (OSHMS) include 
our employees and contractors, of which the number of employees accounts for about 61% and the 
number of contractors accounts for about 39%. 
The management scope covers all workplaces and 
commuting routes for employees. At workplaces, 
contractors receive instructions from employers (or 
those acting on behalf of employers) to handle labor-
related matters.
Each department at FPC formulates an annual 
occupational health and safety management plan, and 
implements health and safety management based on 
the documented procedures and a PDCA model.
In recent years, FPC has been progressively 
integrating AI into occupational health and safety 
management and keeping track of its performance 
with the safety and health performance indicators in 
hopes of shaping a safety culture, thereby building the 
safest work environment in order to achieve the goal 
of "Zero public injury, Zero disaster".
 
Hazard Identification and Risk Assessment
FPC uses organizational and systematic analytical techniques to conduct workplace hazard and risk 
assessments and takes preventive measures accordingly to prevent and improve any unsafe environment 
or behavior during operation. In the event that employees identify any potential hazards and risks in the 
workplace, they can notify their supervisors and are encouraged to report near-misses by filling out the 
"Near-Miss Report Form”. The investigation team will conduct an investigation and file a case to review the 
impact of hazard events and likelihood of occurrence as well as determine the risk level of major potential 
hazards. Then, the team will identify the direct causes, indirect causes, and root causes of near-misses 
by using various types of analysis such as fault tree analysis (FTA). Based on the results from the analysis 
feedback, appropriate revisions will be made to improve standard operating procedures (SOP), process 
conditions, DCS parameters, and other process and operating procedures, so as to strengthen the safety 
of equipment and pipelines at the complexes or to enhance protective and management measures (such 
as key items of self-inspection at the complexes, key points of inspection by supervisors, and production of 
teaching materials for training, etc.).
In 2022, a total of 347 near-miss cases were reported and input into the computer for control and 
improvement. Meanwhile, rewards were issued to encourage employees to continuously and actively identify 
potential hazards and make improvements. Additionally, if employees are in a place where hazards may occur 
or be introduced, employees may use their own judgement and retreat to a place of safety for protection.

Causes of Accidents
The team leaders of each unit which are responsible for performing process hazard analysis (PHA), job 
safety analysis (JSA) and other hazard analysis operations have been trained and certified by the Technical 
Training Center of the Group Administration Office. In addition, some process complexes are Class A or 
Class C hazardous workplaces, and their team leaders have not only passed the aforementioned training 
certification but also obtained the legal process safety assessor certificate and received regular retraining.

126
2022 Formosa Plastics Corporation　Sustainability Report
 
Accident Investigation
FPC has established a complete accident investigation process. Within 32 hours after an accident, an 
accident investigation team is formed according to the scale of the accident to conduct investigation, 
including interviewing relevant personnel and collecting data. Different types of failure analysis, such as 
fault tree analysis (FTA) and failure mode and effects analysis (FMEA), are used to determine the direct, 
indirect, and root causes. After the investigation is completed, the investigation results and improvement 
measures are reported to the President's Office to ensure such an accident does not reoccur.
In addition, each business division assigns employees to receive professional training in major 
investigation management to improve investigation skills. In the event where a cross-company or cross-
plant accident investigation needs to be conducted, appropriate manpower can be assigned to assist in the 
investigation according to the actual situation.

Identiﬁcation of Top 
Ten Risks
In order to strengthen the construction safety of contractors, every day, each complex 
comprehensively screens for top ten high-risk operations and areas with potential 
hazards such as confinement, open flames, elevation (high altitude), water jets, 
high-temperature contact, electricity, lifting and hanging, maintenance and process 
operations, and equipment, and independent inspections are performed by the mid-
level managers. In addition, for high-risk operations and areas with potential hazards, 
supervisors at all levels should go to the construction site to check whether employees 
and contractors are performing operations in accordance with the established standard 
operating procedures (SOP) and job safety analysis (JSA). In 2022, a total of 16,831 
abnormal cases were checked independently, and a total fine of NT$7,930,050 was 
imposed on employees and contractors who violated regulations, where they were also 
required to comply with all regulations for construction operations.
Installation of Pipe 
Rack Inspection 
Walkways
In order to ensure the safety of pipeline inspection personnel, we have planned to install 
inspection walkways in 240 sections of the pipe racks, 134 of which (total 10,519 meters 
in length) have already been completed, and the remaining 106 are expected to be 
improved and completed by the end of June 2025.
Process Hazard 
Analysis (PHA)
In order to strengthen the ability of each complex to identify the hazards of misoperation 
of the process, the process hazard analysis (PHA) was carried out on 116 processes. The 
top three hazards were the start/stop process, normal operations (such as: absorption 
tower regeneration, filter switching) and loading/unloading. In response to the analysis 
results, the operating procedures have been reviewed and revised to improve the safety 
of on-site operations.

Safety and Health Performance Indicators
To monitor and evaluate the safety and health performance of FPC, each department is required to submit 
a report on the implementation of seven safety and health performance indicators every six months. Based 
on the reports, FPC is able to evaluate the safety climate in the entire company and each department, 
diagnose the safety and health management weaknesses, and take corresponding improvement measures.

Description of a PSE Case
After the unloading operation of sulfuric 
acid was completed on April 9, 2022 at the 
Linyuan public utilities complex, when the 
unloading pump stopped, the check valve was 
actuated and created negative pressure at 
the pump outlet, resulting in the sulfuric acid 
not being released due to negative pressure 
siphon effect. On June 25, the on-site staff 
performed the pump steering test by loading 
and unloading the tank truck. However, 
the exhaust valve was not opened prior to 
starting the pump, causing air to enter the 
pipe and relieve the negative pressure. Soon 
after, the residual sulfuric acid in the pipeline 
was pushed to the blind flange, resulting in a 
splash accident.
After the accident, the injured employee was showered and treated with Diphoterine as emergency treatment 
and then was sent to Kaohsiung Chang Gung Memorial Hospital for treatment. The employee was discharged 
from the hospital after 27 days and returned to work.

Improvement measures
Pre-work checks should be implemented.
After the loading/unloading is completed and the pump is stopped, the air valve should be 
opened to ensure that there is no sulfuric acid residue. Also, the blind plate at the end of the 
loading/unloading hose should be blind sealed, and the protective cover securely closed.
In order to avoid residual sulfuric acid, it is recommended to add a hand valve at the inlet of the 
sulfuric acid pump.

Application of AI in Industrial Safety Management
Our Electronic Materials Division has developed an industrial safety management system for expanded 
construction areas based on image recognition technology. Through installing fixed and mobile cameras, 
it is able to identify the wear and use of protective equipment by construction personnel as well as send 
warning alerts to supervisors in real time to assist on-site foremen with industrial safety management. 
Lifting area intrusion detection alert
Personnel violation identification (safety belt not hooked)
 
Care for Employee Health
A. Building a Sound Health Examination and Cloud System
To take care of employees' health, FPC appoints Chang Gung Memorial Hospital to conduct on-site 
health examination for employees at various complexes every year. FPC also includes four types of tests, 
namely "α-fetoprotein test," "carcinoembryonic antigen test," "oral cancer screening," and "static 
electrocardiogram," which is superior to that required by the law.
Additionally, we have also established a medical office at each plant to make it more convenient for 
employees to access services such as preliminary injury diagnosis and treatment, preventive health care, 
weight management, and smoking cessation consultation. Supported by Chang Gung Memorial Hospital 
and its medical resources, we provide medical subsidies to employees and their families to use services 
offered by Chang Gung Memorial Hospital, including deductibles not covered by National Health Insurance 
and discounts for health examinations.
With the intention of encouraging employees to perform health management and improving their physical 
and mental health, FPC has also set up a cloud health management system named "FPC Health Cloud," 
which comes in the form of an app to effectively manage and track employees' health examination results 
and health improvement status. 
B. Prevention of Occupational Diseases
FPC attaches great importance to the occupational health of employees and includes health management, 
abnormality tracking, disease prevention, and hazard assessment for special operations into preventive 
management. Also, FPC provides health education, improvement suggestions, and tracking services. So 
far, no occupational disease cases have occurred.

130
2022 Formosa Plastics Corporation　Sustainability Report
Occupational Disease Prevention Management Items
According to the Tasks with Special Health Hazards described in the Labor Health 
Protection Regulations, FPC has established 12 hazard management items according to the 
industry, process conditions, and workplaces, including noise, ionizing radiation, carbon 
disulfide, n-hexane, vinyl chloride, dust, mercury compounds, formaldehyde, 
dimethylformamide, butadiene, chromic acid and its salts, and manganese and its 
compounds. Our on-site health specialists regularly visit each workplace in accordance with 
the law to assist us in assessing the relationship between the health of special operations 
employees and on-site work as well as conducting preventive work adjustments or 
suitability assessments. Also, we continue to prevent the possibility of occupational diseases 
through mechanisms such as health checks and tracking, individual employee health care 
and consultation, work environment and personal exposure monitoring, etc.
For the second-, third-, and fourth-level personnel on the health management list according 
to the Tasks with Special Health Hazards, a copy of the Health Classification Management 
Reminder Form is sent to carry out health management and control. In 2022, the health 
check rate of special operations employees was 100%.
100% 
Inspection Rate
Special Operation Health Management
A questionnaire on the musculoskeletal symptom is conducted for all employees every 3 
years. In 2022, 7% of the employees who participated in the questionnaire scored 3 points 
or above. Our occupational health specialists were able to provide health education and 
advice on rehabilitation exercises as well as assess the working conditions on site together 
with safety and health management personnel when necessary.
Hazard Assessment and Management of Human Factors
Formulate the "Abnormal Workload-Promoted Disease Prevention Program". Employees can 
fill in the scale of their loading through the online or mobile APP. Based on the physical 
examination data and questionnaire survey results, we determine risk levels and track 
high-risk individuals. Through one-on-one consultation and health education provided by 
occupational health specialists, appropriate adjustments are made to work patterns as needed.
